### BUG: Incorrect `disabled` state for "Push to GitHub" button  
**Severity**: medium  
**Location**: `BuildAction` component, "Push to GitHub" button  
**Problem**: The "Push to GitHub" button's `disabled` prop includes `disabled` from `BuildActionProps`. This means if the overall component is disabled (e.g., due to missing configuration), the push button will also be disabled, even if a build has completed and pushing would otherwise be possible. The `disabled` prop from `BuildActionProps` is intended to disable the *build* action, not necessarily subsequent actions like pushing.  
**Fix**: Remove `disabled` from the `disabled` prop of the "Push to GitHub" button. The button should only be disabled if `!isComplete` or `building`.

### BUG: Incorrect `portable_sed` usage for `safe_dir`  
**Severity**: high  
**Location**: `act4_start_and_register`  
**Problem**: The `portable_sed` function is called with `s#{{INSTALL_DIR}}#${safe_dir}#g` where `safe_dir` is already escaped for `sed` metacharacters. However, `portable_sed` itself uses `sed -i '' "$@"` or `sed -i "$@"`. The `s#...#...#g` syntax uses `#` as a delimiter. If `safe_dir` contains a `#` character, it will prematurely terminate the `sed` command's substitution pattern, leading to a syntax error or incorrect substitution. The current escaping `sed 's/[[\.*^$#&\\\/]/\\&/g'` escapes `#`, which is correct for the `s#...#...#g` delimiter, but the `|` delimiter used for `VERSION` and `SELECTED_GATEWAYS` is not escaped. This creates an inconsistency and potential for issues if `INSTALL_DIR` contains `|`. More critically, the `safe_dir` variable is already escaped for *all* `sed` metacharacters, including the `#` delimiter. When `sed` then tries to interpret `s#{{INSTALL_DIR}}#${safe_dir}#g`, the escaped `#` in `safe_dir` will be treated as a literal `#` and not a delimiter, which is correct. The problem is that the `portable_sed` function itself doesn't handle the delimiter escaping, it just passes the arguments. The current escaping for `safe_dir` is actually *too aggressive* for the `#` delimiter if the intent was for `safe_dir` to be used as a literal string within the replacement part. However, the primary issue is that `portable_sed` is called with different delimiters (`#` and `|`) without ensuring the `safe_dir` is correctly escaped for *all* potential delimiters used in the `sed` calls. The `safe_dir` is escaped for `|` as well, so `portable_sed "s|{{VERSION}}|$VERSION|g"` would also work   

... [3978 more chars truncated]  

</details>

## Model: google/gemini-2.5-flash  
--  
### BUG: Inconsistent Error Handling in `sendServiceResult`  
**Severity**: medium  
**Location**: `sendServiceResult`  
**Problem**: The `sendServiceResult` function checks for `result.error` to determine if an error response should be sent. However, if `result.error` is present, it uses `result.status || 500` for the status code. If `result.error` is *not* present, it uses `result.status || 200`. This means that if a service function returns an error object without a `status` field, it will default to `500`. But if a service function returns a successful result without a `status` field, it will default to `200`. This is inconsistent and could lead to misleading status codes for successful operations that might have a non-200 status (e.g., 201 Created, 204 No Content) but don't explicitly set `result.status`. While the primary issue is with error handling, the default for success should also be explicit if `result.status` is not provided. More critically, if a service returns `result.error` but also `result.data`, the `result.data` is ignored, which might be intended but is worth noting. The main bug is that `result.status` for success defaults to `200` but for error defaults to `500`, which is fine, but the `result.data` is completely ignored if `result.error` is present.  
**Fix**: Ensure that `result.status` is always explicitly set by the service function for both success and error cases, or refine the `sendServiceResult` logic to handle different success status codes more explicitly if `result.data` is present. For now, the most direct fix is to ensure that if `result.error` is present, the `result.data` is not sent, which is already the case. The inconsistency is more about the default status code.  

```typescript
fu

... [3959 more chars truncated]

</details>

  // Any result carrying an error field is treated as an error response,  
  // regardless of whether result.data is also present, to prevent masking errors.  
  if (result.error) {

## Model: google/gemini-2.5-flash  
--  
### BUG: Incorrect default value for ref state  
**Severity**: low  
**Location**: `RepoScanner`  
**Problem**: The `ref` state is initialized to `'main'`, but the `onChange` handler for the ref input field sets it to `'main'` if the event target value is empty. This means if a user types something into the ref field and then deletes it, the `ref` state will correctly become `'main'`. However, if the user never interacts with the ref field and the initial `ref` state is `'main'`, the `trimmedRef` in `handleScan` will also correctly be `'main'`. The issue arises in the `onChange` handler for the ref input: `onChange={(e) => setRef(e.target.value || 'main')}`. If the user types "develop" and then deletes it, `e.target.value` becomes an empty string, and `setRef` is called with `'main'`. This is fine. However, the placeholder text for the ref input is "Branch (main)". If the user wants to explicitly scan the 'main' branch, they might type 'main'. If they then delete 'main', the `ref` state will correctly revert to 'main'. The problem is that the `ref` state is already initialized to `'main'`, so the `|| 'main'` in the `onChange` handler is redundant and could potentially mask issues if the initial state was intended to be an empty string representing "default". While not a critical bug, it's a slight inconsistency.  
**Fix**: The `onChange` handler for the ref input should simply update the state with the input value, and the normalization to 'main' should primarily happen in `handleScan`.  

```typescript
// In RepoScanner component

# <span style="color:#FF9800">🤖 Subagent Transcripts (15)</span>

<details>
<summary><strong>Agent `a05f6dcb046d941ea` (unknown) [42 messages]</strong></summary>

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-03-22 18:36:05]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix bugs in: scripts/remote-install.sh — Read findings from: .rechecker/reports/rck-20260322_183524_611fb3-[LP00002-IT00001-FID00017]-review.md  

Fix ONLY these confirmed bugs (high/medium severity):  

1. **portable_sed delimiter collision** (HIGH): In `act4_start_and_register`, the `portable_sed` call uses `|` as a sed delimiter but `safe_dir` (which is the escaped $INSTALL_DIR) may itself contain `|` chars after escaping, causing sed syntax errors. Fix: change the delimiter from `|` to `#` in the `portable_sed "s|{{INSTALL_DIR}}|${safe_dir}|g"` calls — change to `portable_sed "s#{{INSTALL_DIR}}#${safe_dir}#g"`.  

2. **Multi-line PID from lsof** (MEDIUM): In `act4_start_and_register`, the code does `old_pid=$(lsof -ti:"$PORT" 2>/dev/null)` then `kill "$old_pid"` — if multiple processes bind to the port, lsof outputs multiple PIDs (one per line), and `kill "$old_pid"` fails because it treats the multi-line string as a single invalid arg. Fix: use `kill $old_pid` (unquoted) so shell splits by whitespace: `if [ -n "$old_pid" ]; then kill $old_pid 2>/dev/null || true; fi`.  

3. **Service readiness check too permissive** (HIGH): In `act4_start_and_register`, both `while` loops check readiness with plain `curl ... >/dev/null` which succeeds on any HTTP response (including 404/errors). Fix: align with the initial running check that greps for `'"sessions"'`: `if curl -s "http://localhost:${PORT}/api/sessions" 2>/dev/null | grep -q '"sessions"'; then break; fi`.  

Do NOT fix low-severity issues (yarn output redirection, npm error suppression, git stash, pm2 restart) — those are design choices, not correctness bugs.  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] remote-install-fixes - brief_result"  
- Max 2 lines back to orchestrator  

</div>

Now I can see the exact content. Note that the escaping in `safe_dir` already escapes `|` characters (line 1186: `sed 's/[[\.*^$|&\\\/]/\\&/g'`), which means `safe_dir` will contain `\|` if `INSTALL_DIR` had a `|`. Now I also need to fix the escaping regex itself. Currently on line 1186 the `safe_dir` is built with `sed 's/[[\.*^$|&\\\/]/\\&/g'` which escapes `|`, producing `\|` in `safe_dir`. Let me verify the current escaping and fix it to match the new delimiter:

All fixes are complete and verified:  

1. **Delimiter collision (HIGH)**: Both `portable_sed "s|{{INSTALL_DIR}}|..."` calls in `act4_start_and_register` changed to use `#` as delimiter. The `safe_dir` escaping regex updated to escape `#` instead of `|` (line 1186), so `#` in `INSTALL_DIR` is safely backslash-escaped before being used as the replacement string.  

2. **Multi-line PID (MEDIUM)**: `kill "$old_pid"` changed to `kill $old_pid` (unquoted) so the shell word-splits multiple newline-separated PIDs into separate arguments to `kill`.  

3. **Readiness check too permissive (HIGH)**: Both `while` loop readiness checks changed from `curl ... >/dev/null 2>&1` to `curl ... 2>/dev/null | grep -q '"sessions"'`, matching the same guard already used at the top of `act4_start_and_register`.

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix bugs in: components/plugin-builder/RepoScanner.tsx — Read findings from: .rechecker/reports/rck-20260322_182542_611fb3-[LP00002-IT00001-FID00010]-review.md  

Critical/high bugs to fix:  
1. **Scanning state stuck after abort** (HIGH): In `handleScan` finally block, `if (!signal.aborted) setScanning(false)` leaves scanning=true after abort. Fix: always call `setScanning(false)` in the finally block unconditionally.  
2. **Current url/ref used instead of scanned values** (CRITICAL): Skill addition and selection use current `url`/`ref` state which may have changed after the scan. Fix: Add `scannedUrl`/`scannedRef` state variables, set them after successful scan, use them in `handleAddSkill` and for `key` computation in the skills map.  
3. **ref not trimmed before API call** (MEDIUM): Add `ref.trim() || 'main'` when sending to the API and `onSkillsFound`.  
4. **No unmount cleanup** (MEDIUM): Add a `useEffect` that aborts any in-flight fetch on unmount: `useEffect(() => () => { abortRef.current?.abort() }, [])`.  
5. **React key not unique** (MEDIUM): Change `key={skill.path}` to `key={scannedUrl + ':' + skill.path}` in the skills map.  

Also fix medium issues only if they are genuine bugs (not style/UX preferences).  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] reposcanner-fixes - brief_result"

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix bugs in: services/headless-router.ts — Read findings from: .rechecker/reports/rck-20260322_183524_611fb3-[LP00002-IT00001-FID00018]-review.md  

Fix ONLY these confirmed bugs:  

1. **NaN from invalid query params** (HIGH): Multiple handlers do `parseInt(query.timeout)`, `parseInt(query.limit)`, `parseFloat(query.minConfidence)`, `parseFloat(query.minScore)`, `parseFloat(query.bm25Weight)` etc. If the query param is a non-numeric string, parseInt/parseFloat returns NaN which gets passed to services. Fix: add NaN guards. Create or inline a safe parser: for each `parseInt(query.X)` change to `(query.X && !Number.isNaN(Number(query.X)) ? parseInt(query.X) : undefined)`. Apply this pattern to ALL query param parseInt/parseFloat usages in the file.  

2. **sendServiceResult error condition** (MEDIUM): The `sendServiceResult` function checks `if (result.error && !result.data)` — if both `result.error` and `result.data` are present, it falls through and sends 200 with the data, masking the error. Fix: change the condition to simply `if (result.error)` so any error-bearing result is treated as an error response.  

Do NOT add request body size limits (that's an enhancement, not a bug fix).  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] headless-router-fixes - brief_result"  
- Max 2 lines back to orchestrator

**Old:**  
```
function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {
  if (result.error && !result.data) {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 500, { error: result.error }, result.headers)

    sendJson(res, result.status || 200, result.data, result.headers)

```

**New:**  
```
function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {
  // Any result carrying an error field is treated as an error response,
  // regardless of whether result.data is also present, to prevent masking errors.
  if (result.error) {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 500, { error: result.error }, result.headers)
  } else {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 200, result.data, result.headers)
  }
}
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-611fb3/services/headless-router.ts has been updated successfully.  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 18:36:35]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

**Fix 2: NaN guards for all parseInt/parseFloat usages.** Each one follows the pattern `query.X ? parseInt(query.X) : undefined`. The issue is that a non-numeric string like `"abc"` is truthy and passes the ternary guard, but `parseInt("abc")` returns `NaN`. I'll replace each occurrence with a safe parser that checks `Number.isNaN`:  

</div>

Fix bug in: components/plugin-builder/SkillPicker.tsx  

The `getSkillKey` function for 'repo' type skills uses `skill.skillPath` which does not exist on the PluginSkillSelection type. The correct property is `skill.skillId`.

  `return \`repo:${skill.url}:${skill.skillPath}\``  

Change it to:  
  `return \`repo:${skill.url}:${skill.skillId}\``

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-03-22 18:36:05]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix bugs in: services/plugin-builder-service.ts — Read findings from: .rechecker/reports/rck-20260322_183524_611fb3-[LP00002-IT00001-FID00019]-review.md  

Fix ONLY these confirmed bugs:  

1. **GitHub auth token missing for push** (CRITICAL): In `pushToGitHub`, the code runs `git push origin branch` over HTTPS but provides no authentication credentials. This will always fail for private repos or user forks requiring write access. Fix: The `PluginPushConfig` type (in types/plugin-builder.ts) should have a `token?: string` field. In `pushToGitHub`, before pushing, if a token is provided, set it on the git remote URL: parse the `forkUrl` and inject the token: `const authUrl = forkUrl.replace(/^https:\/\//, \`https://\${config.token}@\`); await execPromise('git', ['remote', 'set-url', 'origin', authUrl], { cwd: pushDir, timeout: 5000 });` then proceed with the push. Only inject credentials if `config.token` is truthy. Also add `token?: string` to the `PluginPushConfig` type in types/plugin-builder.ts.  

2. **Build directory leak on setup failure** (MEDIUM): In `buildPlugin`, `buildId` and `buildDir` are declared with `const` inside the `try` block, making them inaccessible in the `catch` block. If any setup step after `fs.mkdir(buildDir)` fails (writeFile, copyFile, chmod, symlink), the partial directory in BUILDS_DIR is never cleaned up. Fix: declare `let buildId: string | undefined` and `let buildDir: string | undefined` before the try block, then assign them inside the try. In the catch block, add cleanup: `if (buildDir) { fs.rm(buildDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {}); }`.  

3. **activeOps double-decrement** (MEDIUM): If an error occurs in `buildPlugin` between the `activeOps++` and the `runBuild` call, the outer catch decrements `activeOps`, but the `runBuild().finally()` doesn't run — actually this is fine. However, re-read the code carefully and fix any actual double-decrement or missed-decrement of activeOps you find.  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] plugin-builder-service-fixes - brief_result"  
- Max 2 lines back to orchestrator  

</div>

   111→  
   112→function validateGitRef(ref: string): string | null {  
   113→  if (!ref || typeof ref !== 'string') return 'Git ref is required'  
   114→  if (ref.startsWith('-')) return 'Git ref must not start with a dash'  
   115→  if (!GIT_REF_RE.test(ref)) return 'Git ref contains invalid characters'  
   116→  if (ref.includes('..')) return 'Git ref must not contain ".."'  
   117→  return null  
   118→}  
   119→  
   120→function validatePluginName(name: string): string | null {  
   121→  if (!name || typeof name !== 'string') return 'Plugin name is required'  
   122→  if (!PLUGIN_NAME_RE.test(name)) {  
   123→    return 'Plugin name must start with a letter/number and contain only letters, numbers, hyphens, and underscores'  
   124→  }  
   125→  if (name.length > 64) return 'Plugin name too long (max 64 characters)'  
   126→  return null  
   127→}  
   128→  
   129→function validateSkillPath(skillPath: string): string | null {  
   130→  if (!skillPath || typeof skillPath !== 'string') return 'Skill path is required'  
   131→  if (skillPath.includes('..')) return 'Skill path must not contain ".."'  
   132→  if (path.isAbsolute(skillPath)) return 'Skill path must be relative'  
   133→  // Each segment must be safe  
   134→  const segments = skillPath.split('/')

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 18:36:53]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have all the context I need. Let me analyze the three bugs:  

**Bug 1 (Critical):** In `pushToGitHub`, the git push at line 530 uses no authentication. Need to add `token?: string` to `PluginPushConfig` type and inject it into the remote URL before pushing.  

**Bug 2 (Medium):** In `buildPlugin`, `buildId` and `buildDir` are declared with `const` inside the `try` block (lines 324-325), making them inaccessible in the `catch` block (line 383). Partial directories are never cleaned up on setup failure.  

**Bug 3 (Medium - activeOps double-decrement):** Looking at the code carefully:  
- If setup steps fail AFTER `activeOps++` (line 323) and BEFORE `runBuild` is called, the catch block at line 384 decrements `activeOps` — that's correct (once).  
- If `runBuild` is called and throws, the `.catch` handles error, then `.finally()` decrements `activeOps`. The outer catch is NOT reached. That's also correct (once).  
- So there is no actual double-decrement currently. The bug report from the orchestrator says to verify this — it's actually correct. No fix needed for Bug 3.  

Let me now apply the fixes. Starting with the type file and the service file:  

</div>

   556→    }  
   557→  } catch (error: unknown) {  
   558→    await fs.rm(pushDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {})  
   559→    const message = error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)  
   560→    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)  
   561→    return { error: `Failed to push to GitHub: ${message}`, status: 500 }  
   562→  } finally {  
   563→    activeOps = Math.max(0, activeOps - 1)  
   564→  }  
   565→}  
   566→  
   567→// ============================================================================  
   568→// INTERNAL HELPERS  
   569→// ============================================================================  
   570→  
   571→/**  
   572→ * Run build-plugin.sh in the build directo  

... [1015 more chars truncated]

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The `portable_sed` call uses single quotes around the sed expression, preventing `${PORT}` from expanding. The fix is to use double quotes so the shell expands `${PORT}` before passing it to `sed`. Note that `|` is the sed delimiter here, so no special concern with slashes. The `.*` in the pattern and the replacement are not shell-significant so double-quoting is safe:  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 18:19:58]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The shellcheck SC2086 warning is specifically about word splitting/globbing when a variable is unquoted in a command. In a URL like `http://localhost:${PORT}/api/sessions`, the `${PORT}` is inside a larger string argument to curl — it's already part of a single word, so it won't split. However, shellcheck still warns when the variable isn't double-quoted inside the string. The flagged lines from the lint report are: 1105, 1126, 1161, 1198, 1233 (original line numbers). These correspond to the curl command lines at current lines 1102, 1123, 1158, 1195, 1230.  

The fix per shellcheck's suggestion is `http://localhost:"${PORT}"/api/sessions`. Let me apply these 5 fixes:  

</div>

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-03-22 18:48:50]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix bugs in: services/headless-router.ts — Read findings from: .rechecker/reports/rck-20260322_184524_611fb3-[LP00002-IT00002-FID00018]-review.md  

Fix ONLY these confirmed bugs:  

1. **parseMultipart latin1 data corruption** (HIGH): The `parseMultipart` function converts the entire body buffer to a `latin1` string then splits it, and converts file parts back using `Buffer.from(content, 'latin1')`. This works for binary files but is fragile. The real bug is that there is no boundary check if `contentType` is missing or malformed — `parseMultipart` will crash or return bad data. Also if the boundary match fails, `boundaryMatch` is null and the function returns `{ file: null, options: null }`. The handler then calls `if (!file)` which catches it. This part is OK. The actual correctness bug: after splitting, `part.replace(/\r\n$/, '')` removes one CRLF but the binary data reconstruction via `Buffer.from(content, 'latin1')` may lose data if the part content itself has `\r\n\r\n` sequences that split the headers incorrectly. Fix: Make the latin1 → Buffer conversion safe by also checking for double-CRLF header separator more carefully. Specifically, ensure the part content split on `\r\n\r\n` only splits on the FIRST occurrence: change `const [headers, content] = part.split('\r\n\r\n')` to `const headerEnd = part.indexOf('\r\n\r\n'); if (headerEnd === -1) return acc; const headers = part.slice(0, headerEnd); const content = part.slice(headerEnd + 4);` (and remove the trailing `\r\n` from content: `content.replace(/\r\n$/, '')`).  

2. **Missing await for synchronous service calls** (MEDIUM): Handlers for `GET /api/config` and `GET /api/organization` call `sendServiceResult(res, getSystemConfig())` and `sendServiceResult(res, getOrganization())` without `await`. If these functions are async or become async, the Promise would be passed to sendServiceResult instead of the resolved value. Fix: Add `await` before the service calls: `sendServiceResult(res, await getSystemConfig())` and `sendServiceResult(res, await getOrganization())`.  

Do NOT re-fix the `sendServiceResult` condition (already fixed to check `result.error` only). Do NOT change the latin1 encoding approach entirely (that's a larger refactor).  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] headless-router-it2-fixes - brief_result"  
- Max 2 lines back to orchestrator  

</div>

   340→ * Handles the single use case: one file field + one text field for /api/agents/import.

   342→function parseMultipart(body: Buffer, contentType: string): { file: Buffer | null; options: string | null } {  
   343→  const boundaryMatch = contentType.match(/boundary=([^\s;]+)/)  
   344→  if (!boundaryMatch) return { file: null, options: null }  
   345→  
   346→  const boundary = '--' + boundaryMatch[1]  
   347→  const bodyStr = body.toString('latin1')  
   348→  const parts = bodyStr.split(boundary).slice(1, -1) // Remove preamble and epilogue  
   349→  
   350→  let file: Buffer | null = null  
   351→  let options: string | null = null  
   352→  
   353→  for (const part of parts) {  
   354→    const headerEnd = part.indexOf('\r\n\r\n')  
   355→    if (headerEnd === -1) continue  
   356→  
   357→    const headers = part.substring(0, headerEnd)  
   358→    const content = part.substring(headerEnd + 4).replace(/\r\n$/, '')  
   359→  
   360→    if (headers.includes('name="file"')) {  
   361→      // Convert back to buffer from latin1 encoding  
   362→      file = Buffer.from(content, 'latin1')  
   363→    } else if (headers.includes('name="options"')) {  
   364→      options = content  
   365→    }  
   366→  }  
   367→  
   368→  return { file, options }  
   369→}  
   370→

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 18:49:16]*

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 18:35:02]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `route.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-611fb3/app/api/plugin-builder/build/route.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  try {
    const body = await request.json()
    const result = await buildPlugin(body)

    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data, { status: result.status })
  } catch {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Invalid request body' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  // Parse JSON separately so SyntaxError returns 400, not 500
  let body: unknown
  try {
    body = await request.json()
  } catch {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Invalid request body' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }

  try {
    const result = await buildPlugin(body)

    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data, { status: result.status })
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error building plugin:', error)
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Internal server error' },
      { status: 500 }
    )
  }
}
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-611fb3/app/api/plugin-builder/build/route.ts has been updated successfully.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 18:35:05]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The bug is on line 214. `skill.id.split(':')[2]` is unsafe because if the id has fewer than 3 colon-separated segments, it returns `undefined`, making the `|| skill.id` fallback the only safety net — but when the segment exists yet is empty string, `split(':').pop()` is more semantically correct and always defined. The fix per the findings is to use `.split(':').pop() || skill.id`.  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 18:35:06]*

<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `PluginComposer.tsx`</summary>

**Old:**  
```
    case 'marketplace':
      return skill.id.split(':')[2] || skill.id
```

**New:**  
```
    case 'marketplace':
      // Use .pop() to safely get the last segment regardless of how many colons the id contains
      return skill.id.split(':').pop() || skill.id
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-611fb3/components/plugin-builder/PluginComposer.tsx has been updated successfully.
